  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f7183230-8ff4-45fa-8f37-028fe25972a5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    I think it's to show the fear that an abused woman feels no matter where her abuser might be. You always live with that "what if" scenario in your head. I don't believe Ian is alive, but the fear will always be there.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236239207" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9051472817812260599">WOW! <br/><br/>I just finished this book about 10 minutes ago and I'm very impressed. I'm also very tired as it's now after 5am! I will be so very tired today but it is totally worth it!!<br/><br/>I have so many good books that I want to read right now. I keep adding to my collection faster than I'm reading. I've gotten into a bad habit of reading a couple of pages of new books and forgetting which one I wanted to read next. Because of that this novel had been forgotten about until today. When I picked it up again </span>
  <span id="freeText9051472817812260599" style="display:none">WOW! <br /><br />I just finished this book about 10 minutes ago and I'm very impressed. I'm also very tired as it's now after 5am! I will be so very tired today but it is totally worth it!!<br /><br />I have so many good books that I want to read right now. I keep adding to my collection faster than I'm reading. I've gotten into a bad habit of reading a couple of pages of new books and forgetting which one I wanted to read next. Because of that this novel had been forgotten about until today. When I picked it up again today I did find it a little bit hard to get into at first but once I was a little ways in I was hooked! <br /><br />Jenna the main character is desperate to escape from her past after a tragic hit-and-run accident destroys her life. Feeling lost she finds her way to a small Welsh community where she attempts to pick up the pieces and start anew. She is haunted by her fear and grief. Memories pulling her back and forcing her to face things that cannot be ignored. Investigator Ray Stevens and his team work hard to seek justice for a mother who is living every parent's worst nightmare. <br /><br />This psychological thriller had me captivated and I really was unable to put it down until I finished it. An emotional plot with a huge twist that snuck right up on me making my heart jump into my throat. Completely changed the dynamic of the story and then another twist that I never expected. Many great characters that are very well developed. Jenna is haunting and felt very authentic as did many of the characters. This novel clearly shows how in one moment an unexpected tragedy can occur leaving many people devastated. <br /><br />I think I'll stop there as I don't want to give anything away. This was such a great debut novel and I'm excited to read more from Clare Mackintosh!! <br />Highly recommended!!! <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1284071598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1284071598" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1284071598?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23534398-i-let-you-go">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=not-impressed">not-impressed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1284071598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957967877746437790">Jacob, a five year old boy is killed at the start of the novel. <br/>NOTHING PLEASANT SO FAR! Then for the next 400 or so pages -- we feel nothing for this poor child. We never knew him to begin with. His death is a shock incident - we have no emotional connection with him whatsoever. So... the story is about 'who killed him?" why did the driver hit Jacob and drive away? And why the hell after a year, are there no leads about the case? And why is it taking so long to tell this story--when 'some' of u</span>
  <span id="freeText9957967877746437790" style="display:none">Jacob, a five year old boy is killed at the start of the novel. <br />NOTHING PLEASANT SO FAR! Then for the next 400 or so pages -- we feel nothing for this poor child. We never knew him to begin with. His death is a shock incident - we have no emotional connection with him whatsoever. So... the story is about 'who killed him?" why did the driver hit Jacob and drive away? And why the hell after a year, are there no leads about the case? And why is it taking so long to tell this story--when 'some' of us (me), can see the ending -in the first 20% of this book? <br /><br />"A sculptor not sculpting .....and a mother without a child". <br />NOTHING TOO INSPIRING ABOUT THAT..... (about JENNA). Our main character, Jenna, is the sculptor, no longer sculpting and mother without a child. <br />Jenna is intended as a sympathetic character....but mostly I found her passive and irritating. Her little boy dies - yet within three months she is "feeling alive" drawing her name in the sand, taking photos with her camera on the beach. YOU'VE GOT TO BE KIDDING!! FISHY FISHY FISHY!! She runs away - goes off grid - throws her cell phone away -hides out- - 'less' that 3 months after her child is killed. In 6 months she's happy about a new photography business? Odd!!! She is completely out of communication with the police Dept - the people who are trying to find HER son's killer . They have no idea where she is living or how to reach her for much of the book. <br />......Jenna's new boyfriend is one hell of a dandy cherry pie, too! <br />.....The entire plot was implausible. <br />.....Lots of coincidences- unbelievable - insane - absurd! <br />......Yucky uninspiring male characters<br />......The 'side-story' of the detectives teenage son-- shows 'more' uninspiring 'men'. The author even managed to turned a 12 year old BOY into an uninspiring character. <br />He wouldn't win any young male roll model awards - that's for sure. <br /><br />......Throughout the tale, Jenna was constantly referring to her breathing: "I couldn't catch my breath", "my breathing became"..."I felt my breath.." <br />I'm 'not' exaggerating, when I say there were so many references to "breathing", it became annoying. I know nothing about editing...but I would have caught the 'breathing' ( authors blind spot), repetitive phrases. But it drove me crazy. I almost started counting how many more times I'd have to hear Jenna talk about her breathing. <br /><br />.....Not only did I see the the 'mystery-ending' very early into this novel- [I found it very predictable], but there was so much 'yuckiness' about this novel... I didn't feel inspired about myself for having read it. <br />.....While listening to this audiobook - during hikes, soaking in the pool, on car rides to the beach with Paul in the car...( even Paul figured out the ending - by only listening to parts of this book)....I kept thinking...."this is 2016, a contemporary story"....<br />"We need stories about strong female characters - not weak ones". <br />"Shame on me for getting sucked into this book" - it's nasty!!<br /><br />There was not one character in this entire book to be inspired about...<br />...A kid is killed : hit and run<br />...The police dept. Is dysfunctional - each with personal problems - home problems- <br />...everyone is a victim! <br />....Abuse, violence, lies, cheating, silly&amp; boring...<br />... Yucky is as Yucky is! I want my money back!!!!<br /><br />2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9957967877746437790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1138687790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138687790" />
    <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady"><img alt="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601761303p2/22943325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138687790?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady">Maxine (Booklover Catlady)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23534398-i-let-you-go">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=psychological-thrillers-read">psychological-thrillers-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=maxines-favourites">maxines-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=could-not-put-down">could-not-put-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138687790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16889353648146539365">I love a good psychological thriller, and this one fell into the category of excellent ones. Holy macaroni Batman! <b>I did NOT see that twist coming in a million years!</b> I just stared at the page whilst my brain scrambled to get some footing again. And it wasn't the only one. But the BIGGIE was done so very, very well. <br/><br/><i>A tragic accident. It all happened so quickly. She couldn't have prevented it. Could she?<br/><br/>In a split second, Jenna Gray's world descends into a nightmare. Her only hope of moving on i</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16889353648146539365" style="display:none">I love a good psychological thriller, and this one fell into the category of excellent ones. Holy macaroni Batman! <b>I did NOT see that twist coming in a million years!</b> I just stared at the page whilst my brain scrambled to get some footing again. And it wasn't the only one. But the BIGGIE was done so very, very well. <br /><br /><i>A tragic accident. It all happened so quickly. She couldn't have prevented it. Could she?<br /><br />In a split second, Jenna Gray's world descends into a nightmare. Her only hope of moving on is to walk away from everything she knows to start afresh. Desperate to escape, Jenna moves to a remote cottage on the Welsh coast, but she is haunted by her fears, her grief and her memories of a cruel November night that changed her life forever.<br /><br />Slowly, Jenna begins to glimpse the potential for happiness in her future. But her past is about to catch up with her, and the consequences will be devastating...</i><br /><br /><b>It's so hard to talk anymore about the plot of this book without giving away the entire reason for the book so I am not going to do that.</b> <br /><br />All I will say is that the plot is cleverly written, with twists that I have already told you are amazing and plenty more surprise moments along the way. It's very clever with the way stories intertwine like rope to make for a very strong book overall. Fascinating. I was flicking pages wanting more of the story to reveal itself.<br /><br />The characters in the book I thought were excellent, I felt I could relate to each of them as if I was there with them, in the story, including the peripheral characters as well. Some might find a bit of a hate/love with Jenna I think, for me, I reserved judgement on her until the end of the book. <br /><br />It has some tense, thrilling and shocking moments in it, some you see coming, some you don't, but it's not a boring book by any means. I could not put it down once I got going and was so thrilled that it took me to places I did not predict it would. I had heard good things about this one but went in with no expectations. <br /><br /><b>All in all, a stunning and sometimes surprising novel with a powerful message running through it, a book that will quench your thirst for a novel you can at last just sink into and lose yourself completely. A book you will recommend to all your friends.</b> <br /><br />An easy five star read for me and one that has gone on my favourite's shelf. Nice work from Clare Mackintosh, I will be looking for more of her work in the future. <br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Many thanks.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16889353648146539365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1759267022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1759267022" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1759267022?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759267022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8036601653847590383">I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh is a 2016 Berkley publication. <br/><br/><br/>I heard so many good things about this book, by the time I got my hands on a copy I was frothing at the mouth with excitement. Did the book live up to all the hype? <br/><br/>Oh yeah, it’s very clever! The one downside is that it is hard to say much of anything at all about the plot, so I will refer you back to the book synopsis/blurb to get the setup. <br/><br/>I did have a few issues with a couple of lead characters, but since no one is mentioning th</span>
  <span id="freeText8036601653847590383" style="display:none">I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh is a 2016 Berkley publication. <br /><br /><br />I heard so many good things about this book, by the time I got my hands on a copy I was frothing at the mouth with excitement. Did the book live up to all the hype? <br /><br />Oh yeah, it’s very clever! The one downside is that it is hard to say much of anything at all about the plot, so I will refer you back to the book synopsis/blurb to get the setup. <br /><br />I did have a few issues with a couple of lead characters, but since no one is mentioning that part of the story, I won’t either. Other than that, I was impressed with this debut thriller, which lures you in with a heart wrenching situation, quietly and slowly, but despite the low key pacing, the mystery deepens as you go along, becoming more curious and puzzling, and the last quarter of the book was absolutely riveting with one huge, shocking gut punch you will not see coming, which also comes with a few aftershocks. <br /><br />So despite the understated quality the book begins with, by the time you finish the book you might experience a little mental exhaustion.<br /><br />Although I hate writing such a vague review when I feel the need to discuss the characters and my personal opinion of them, and would like to have the opportunity to drop a few clues that would compel someone to give the book a try, I can tell you that if you like psychological thrillers and mysteries you will most likely appreciate this one and the cunning technique of the author employs. <br /><br />Overall, this one gets kudos for originality, for tossing the formula writing out the window and for giving me a story that challenged me, which is just what I am always on the lookout for. 4 stars<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8036601653847590383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17495130678517364469">Thought I was finished reading for the night but decided that I just had to finish this one! While I had it all figured out early on, it didn't keep me from enjoying this one. Extremely well written debut and I look forward to her next book.<br/><br/>Jacob is a 5 year old little boy who lets go of his mother's hand for a brief moment and is killed in a hit and run in the prologue of this gripping police procedural. Jenna Gray's life is forever changed and runs away immediately following the accident to es</span>
  <span id="freeText17495130678517364469" style="display:none">Thought I was finished reading for the night but decided that I just had to finish this one! While I had it all figured out early on, it didn't keep me from enjoying this one. Extremely well written debut and I look forward to her next book.<br /><br />Jacob is a 5 year old little boy who lets go of his mother's hand for a brief moment and is killed in a hit and run in the prologue of this gripping police procedural. Jenna Gray's life is forever changed and runs away immediately following the accident to escape the talk of the town.<br /><br />This book felt almost like 2 separate books between "Part one" and "Part two". I found myself not totally engrossed until I reached "Part two", but once I hit that I couldn't put this down! I really enjoyed the author's note at the end which explained how this story came about; its real life influences from her work as a police official and personal, family experiences as well. I think if I had been able to go in blind on this one and not been told time and again of "the big twist(s)" it would have gotten me; however, because I was expecting them I found myself figuring it all out before the reveals. This book was still extremely enjoyable for me regardless of the twists; I always enjoy a book more if it can stand on its own without the gimmicks. The characters were strong and believable; this book was well-developed all around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17495130678517364469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1138491029216231633"><b>I Let You Go</b> is incredibly cliche and predictable, the format of the book was so familiar because a lot of thrillers seem to follow the same trend.It's all muddled at the start,then we get to about the halfway point and there's a "big twist"or revelation and the book is switching between the past and present to eventually uncover the mystery.<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[And then the bad guy(in this case the abusive husband,Ian) comes back and gives the protagonist,Jenna one last beating. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was</span>
  <span id="freeText1138491029216231633" style="display:none"><b>I Let You Go</b> is incredibly cliche and predictable, the format of the book was so familiar because a lot of thrillers seem to follow the same trend.It's all muddled at the start,then we get to about the halfway point and there's a "big twist"or revelation and the book is switching between the past and present to eventually uncover the mystery.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And then the bad guy(in this case the abusive husband,Ian) comes back and gives the protagonist,Jenna one last beating. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was expecting a massive,exciting twist,it wasn't,it was stupid and so underwhelming.<br /><br />The first half of the book before the twist is exciting and I mostly enjoyed that half.To be fair, the writing is great, it's the story and charcters that dragged the book's rating down for me.There is some fantastic descriptions in this book, especially when the author descibes the crash scene and the writing never left me confused and it wasn't too basic.<br /><br />The detectives were so boring, I hated when it switched back to Ray, I much preferred Jenna's narrative.The plot wasn't really exciting and then they were other small reveals throughout the story which were so predictable or just unnecessary,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like the bit where it turns out Jacob was Ian's son just seemed so pointless and was only thrown in for shock value. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I thought the ending was just plain stupid because the police were idiots.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They leave Jenna go home, without any police protection and don't even arrange for someone to watch her house or check up on her when she returns home to an incredibly remote area in Wales where she has no neighbours and Ian could easily find her which he does and proceeds to beat her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>This ending was soooo cliche and I instantly knew what was going to happen.<br /><br />I somewhat enjoyed the first part of this novel and the writing along with the descriptions but would I recommend this book?Absolutely not and I'm annoyed I bought it, quick read though.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2226632049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9697390112409454286">I stayed up late last night to finish this one - which speaks volumes about how much I was enjoying it, as I value my sleep more than anything else in life!<br/><br/>A young mum walks her 5 year old son home from school, like any other day. Except that this day is different, her son lets go of her hand and is hit by a car and killed instantly.<br/>In Part 1 we flick between two POVs - that of the woman, choosing to begin her life again after the horrific accident and grief it has left behind. She moves from Br</span>
  <span id="freeText9697390112409454286" style="display:none">I stayed up late last night to finish this one - which speaks volumes about how much I was enjoying it, as I value my sleep more than anything else in life!<br /><br />A young mum walks her 5 year old son home from school, like any other day. Except that this day is different, her son lets go of her hand and is hit by a car and killed instantly.<br />In Part 1 we flick between two POVs - that of the woman, choosing to begin her life again after the horrific accident and grief it has left behind. She moves from Bristol to rural South Wales, a place where no one knows her, or her past.<br />The second POV is the Bristol Police Force. Ray - the DI for the CID team is trying to juggle his workload with his family life, and it is proving difficult. He spends more and more time at work to escape the stress of his home life. When the death of 5 year old Jacob comes to their attention Ray is determined to discover who did it, and why they drove away from the scene of the crime.<br /><br />Full of twists and turns, I was gripped by the storyline. I did get a brief sense of deja vu - as I read a book last year <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7575266.The_Bed_I_Made" title="The Bed I Made by Lucie Whitehouse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bed I Made</a> which also involves a young woman who moves to a secluded area to escape her past. But I guess that's quite a popular trope in the mystery/thriller genre.<br /><br />I liked the different POVs - even though one of them was absolutely terrifying to read about. I was sufficiently thrilled - so I guess the book did its job! 4 stars!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9697390112409454286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1149369557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149369557" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149369557?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Janet 5, compelling review.
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149369557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13351391122420489454">I Let You Go is a very smart, very clever psychological mystery by new British author Clare Mackintosh. This is an extremely impressive debut novel.<br/><br/>The story involves a hit and run killing of a 5-year-old boy and is told from the POV of 3 characters—our main protagonist Jenna, the lead detective on the case Ray, and a man named Ian. Ms. Mackintosh is an excellent writer. She knows how to capture the reader’s attention right off the bat. Jenna and Ray are well characterized and Ms. Mackintosh had</span>
  <span id="freeText13351391122420489454" style="display:none">I Let You Go is a very smart, very clever psychological mystery by new British author Clare Mackintosh. This is an extremely impressive debut novel.<br /><br />The story involves a hit and run killing of a 5-year-old boy and is told from the POV of 3 characters—our main protagonist Jenna, the lead detective on the case Ray, and a man named Ian. Ms. Mackintosh is an excellent writer. She knows how to capture the reader’s attention right off the bat. Jenna and Ray are well characterized and Ms. Mackintosh had me rooting mightily for both, though they each had flaws. Jenna, in particular, I cared deeply about. Ian, on the other hand, I abhorred. He is absolutely loathsome, and I was disappointed every time one of his chapters appeared. <br /><br />The highlight of the story for me was the gobsmacking twist (more like a tornado) that hit just before the halfway mark. Wowzers!!!! I do believe this was one of if not THE biggest twist I have ever come across in my fictional reading. I was momentarily disoriented as I went back to reread the paragraph a couple of times before I was convinced that what I thought I had read was indeed what I did read. This was by all means not the end of the surprises, but it sure packed the most powerful punch!<br /><br />Other positives included an interesting side story involving Ray’s family life, which held my interest, though I wasn’t certain I totally bought into a situation with his young son. I did think the police procedural part of the book was well done, especially considering this is primarily a psychological thriller. Ms. Mackintosh, being a former detective herself, is clearly well qualified to write a believable crime story. I also thought she did a particularly terrific job with the complex psychological aspects of the story--well done for a non-psychologist! Clearly this reflects her willingness to do her homework.<br /><br />So why 4 stars instead of 5? I marked down the rating for strictly personal reasons. I have recently read several books that feature despicable male characters that abuse women. I have found myself becoming less and less tolerant of that situation, and stories that spotlight that angle have become much less attractive to me. Let me go on to say, however, that I am sure my position on this is not the norm amongst psychological thriller fans, and it does not keep me from recommending the novel.<br /><br />I highly recommend I Let You Go for all fans of psychological suspense. I think it is an outstanding novel, especially for a debut author. I eagerly await Ms. Mackintosh’s next offering. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13351391122420489454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1903859212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903859212" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903859212?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1903859212&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1903859212" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3984613275989864037">I do my best to always keep my reviews relatively spoiler-free. Hell, most of the time I barely even comment on the plot at all. I don't usually provide my own synopsis or rehash any major bits of the story. However, I feel like with this book I need to dive into the plot and discuss more of the details because, man, I had a really complicated relationship with this book. So anyway... fair warning. Don't read beyond here if you haven't read the book yet. Hey, if you haven't read it yet, come bac</span>
  <span id="freeText3984613275989864037" style="display:none">I do my best to always keep my reviews relatively spoiler-free. Hell, most of the time I barely even comment on the plot at all. I don't usually provide my own synopsis or rehash any major bits of the story. However, I feel like with this book I need to dive into the plot and discuss more of the details because, man, I had a really complicated relationship with this book. So anyway... fair warning. Don't read beyond here if you haven't read the book yet. Hey, if you haven't read it yet, come back here after you finish it. Let's discuss it. Let me know how you feel. <br /><br />Actually, you can read this paragraph, too, before things get more detailed. I should preface this by saying I went into reading I Let You Go knowing very little about the plot except the major event that happens at the very beginning. I also went into it thinking it would likely be like a better version of Gone Girl or The Girl on the Train or something else with Girl in the title. I thought it could probably be called The Girl Who Let Go or I Let the Girl Go since it felt like it would be like any of those kinds of books. So that's where my head was at when I cracked into this bad boy. <br /><br />OK - stop here if you haven't read it. Final warning. <br /><br />Part I of I Let You Go is fantastic. I loved the bouncing back and forth between Jacob being hit by a car and Jenna running away to the story of the cops trying to figure out what happened and searching for leads. It was a nice slow burn and there were subtle things happening to develop the story and the characters. The dynamic of Ray and Kate was awkward and you could see early on where it was going, but it never went over the top. Jenna taking off to a remote location and starting over was great to read about as she met new people and tried to build a new life. Not a whole lot going on. Cops would always hit a dead end. Jenna would drink coffee and build relationships. I liked it through. I was cool with it. <br /><br />Then I hit that last page before Part II where you find out Jenna isn't Jacob's mom and she was driving (for now). I threw the book down and looked over at my wife and said, "Oh my God! Are you gonna read this?! No, you aren't gonna read this because a kid dies at the beginning. No way you are reading this. Anyway...". And I broke down al that just happened and how it all got flipped on its head right there at the end of Part I. I loved the beginning. And,man, like I said, I didn't know much about the book so I'm just along for the ride just happy to be surprised and twisted around a little bit. I liked where things were going. <br /><br />Part II was a bit of a letdown for me though. Yeah, I know. This was your favorite part of the book. You took your foot off the brakes and just plowed through the second half of the book. I read your review. I know what's up. And I can completely see why you would do that because Part II was insane! It was wild and crazy and outta control! I flew right the hell through it, too! I'm with you! <br /><br />Ian ruined this book for me though. Ian took what was going so well and brought everything back into the muddy world of those books I mentioned earlier. Ian was that guy from You by Caroline Kepnes just recast into a different world. That garbage is so played out though. Normal guy who is actually a controlling psycho. I'm over it. Every chapter with him pissed me off. It ruined the momentum of the story. He even talked from the same perspective as that Kepnes book. You did this. You did that. Look at you. And he does all this stupid stuff to Jenna that just didn't work. Ian ruined it. It could have been so much more if she didn't add Ian and his character I'm sick of reading about. <br /><br />The rest of the plot twists and things were fine. There were some interesting surprises, and Ian needed to be there to get to some of those conclusions, but it was just too much of an abrasive turn from where the book was heading in the first half. So I said it ruined it, but it's still a three star read for me. Still a cut above others it will be compared to in the genre. It just could have been more, and I wish I could say it was. I just can't do anymore psycho guy going psycho on a woman physically and emotionally. But it's working. And now the book has to fall back and be compared to other polarizing Girl whatever books. <br /><br />I did like the author's note at the end with her background of what inspired the story. It couldn't have been an easy book for her to write, and I am cool with reading whatever she does next. After this become a movie, of course. This will definitely be a movie. <br /><br />And Ian will ruin it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3984613275989864037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1202383831" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1202383831?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1202383831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13965814912985585260">I received a copy of I Let You Go through NetGalley. Thank you to NetGalley, Sphere Books, and to Clare Mackintosh for the opportunity.<br/><br/>In a matter of seconds lives will change forever.<br/><br/>A distracted mother follows behind her five year old son after picking him up from school on a rainy afternoon. Jacob is joyful upon the promise of a fun afternoon with his mom. He leaps one foot in front of the other chasing that promise into the street and into an oncoming car. The impact has tragic results. Gone</span>
  <span id="freeText13965814912985585260" style="display:none">I received a copy of I Let You Go through NetGalley. Thank you to NetGalley, Sphere Books, and to Clare Mackintosh for the opportunity.<br /><br />In a matter of seconds lives will change forever.<br /><br />A distracted mother follows behind her five year old son after picking him up from school on a rainy afternoon. Jacob is joyful upon the promise of a fun afternoon with his mom. He leaps one foot in front of the other chasing that promise into the street and into an oncoming car. The impact has tragic results. Gone is a young life and gone are the hope-filled days of a young mother.<br /><br />In the aftermath, Jenna struggles with the pressing desire to leave the city as quickly as possible and boards a bus to wherever the rolling of the wheels may take her. Perhaps Wales is far enough away from the heartache. In a final motion, she drops her cell phone into a puddle cutting ties with the strings of her past life. Jenna walks away from her days as a successful sculptor and her career as an artist.<br /><br />The seashore beckons Jenna with its blustery winds as she comes upon a tiny rental cabin not far from the shore. Jenna makes friends with Iestyn, the owner of a small store within the town. Iestyn keeps a special eye on Jenna and senses a deep sorrow.<br /><br />In time, Jenna retrieves her camera from her backpack and begins to photograph the beauty of the tide. Her talent is noticed by the local vet, Patrick Mathews, and they become friends. Is life finally returning to Jenna in small stages?<br /><br />But the calm and the peacefulness are short-lived. Someone is searching for Jenna. Someone who hardly has her best interest in mind. The clues are only recognizable to Jenna herself. She is no longer safe within this once distant sanctuary.<br /><br />And there are mind games and a twist that may tie you up into a cramped knot. This is a very well written book by Clare Mackintosh who knows how to snap out a good ol' "gotcha" from the darkness underneath those stairs of your guarded mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13965814912985585260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288287477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10065601608474496192">A really good thriller. A teenie bit slow in the middle, where I was rushing to get through it, just so I could move along to my next read. But then, it picked up pace and I kept stopping at the end so the end would not come. Sounds like I couldn't make up my mind?! But a definite 5 star read. A hit and run, followed by lots of twists and turns as we follow the unexpected path of the unexpected party. The Welsh countryside was a joy to read about, the ocean sounds wonderful there, even if so ver</span>
  <span id="freeText10065601608474496192" style="display:none">A really good thriller. A teenie bit slow in the middle, where I was rushing to get through it, just so I could move along to my next read. But then, it picked up pace and I kept stopping at the end so the end would not come. Sounds like I couldn't make up my mind?! But a definite 5 star read. A hit and run, followed by lots of twists and turns as we follow the unexpected path of the unexpected party. The Welsh countryside was a joy to read about, the ocean sounds wonderful there, even if so very different to the sunny summers of Sydney. Bethan was a character I loved to read about, I always notice the ones that are good inside. Loved the way she took good care. The policing aspect was a bit annoying, too many acronyms for me, and also the teaming of the DI and other detective on her way up was a bit forced. I didn't enjoy reading about them as much as I did Jenna, and her time in Wales. This is a great read if you do get the chance. My read very nearly didn't happen, my library made a huge mistake on cataloguing this one. I'm not the best cataloguer but I wouldn't make that mistake! Great book. Love being hooked like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10065601608474496192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340428282" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8048008413270080674">Lately it seems like every suspense or psychological thriller is compared to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a>. I often wonder if Gillian Flynn is excited to see so many comparisons to her work, so many people trying to emulate that shock value or if she feels that most don’t live up to the epic twist that made <i>Gone Girl</i> so special, like I do. <br/><br/>I’m excited to say - this is one book that actually lives up to that comparison. Don't get me wrong, this is an entirely different story, but it delivers that same level of shock</span>
  <span id="freeText8048008413270080674" style="display:none">Lately it seems like every suspense or psychological thriller is compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>. I often wonder if Gillian Flynn is excited to see so many comparisons to her work, so many people trying to emulate that shock value or if she feels that most don’t live up to the epic twist that made <i>Gone Girl</i> so special, like I do. <br /><br />I’m excited to say - this is one book that actually lives up to that comparison. Don't get me wrong, this is an entirely different story, but it delivers that same level of shock. The best way to describe this book - <b>
  <i>clever.</i>
</b> From start to finish, the storyline is compelling, unexpected and full of great twists. You might think you know what's happening and how the characters are involved, but in reality, <b>you have no clue</b>. It's something totally different altogether, making it so worth the read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6064606667382056016">And just like that, Mackintosh is redeemed in my eyes!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560857096ra/27686980.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Artist, Jenna Gray, arrives in a small town on the Welsh Coast and hastily rents a remote cottage. <br/><br/>Like many unreliable narrators before her, she is clearly running from something, but what?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548713663ra/26982765.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Chances are it is connected with the hit-and-run death of a child that the book opens with, but as a reader, you aren't sure of the connection to Jenna.<br/><br/>We then follow her as she settles into her new life and begins to find happiness in her newly discovered</span>
  <span id="freeText6064606667382056016" style="display:none">And just like that, Mackintosh is redeemed in my eyes!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560857096ra/27686980.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Artist, Jenna Gray, arrives in a small town on the Welsh Coast and hastily rents a remote cottage. <br><br>Like many unreliable narrators before her, she is clearly running from something, but what?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548713663ra/26982765.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Chances are it is connected with the hit-and-run death of a child that the book opens with, but as a reader, you aren't sure of the connection to Jenna.<br><br>We then follow her as she settles into her new life and begins to find happiness in her newly discovered independence. Simultaneously, we follow intrepid police detectives continuing to work the hit-and-run case.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561559882ra/27729616.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Slowly, the two storylines begin to merge and what is revealed projects the narrative into the stratosphere. <br><br>A new perspective is introduced and things rapidly start to come together.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561559882ra/27729617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had a lot of fun with this one, although some of the subject matter was hard to read. <br><br><u>Trigger Warnings for</u>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[spousal abuse (physical and emotional) ON PAGE, death of a child, and miscarriage caused by violence. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, I loved the atmosphere, the mystery was strong, as well as the police procedural aspects of the story. Jenna really grew on me over the course of the book and all in all, I did appreciate her character growth.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588165768ra/29376252.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would recommend this to the few thriller readers out there who have yet to pick it up.     <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3332895-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418165902p2/3332895.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1252131719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13937240143189792338">**If you haven't read this book, I recommend you not read reviews until you have finished the book. If you disregard my suggestion, please don't read my spoiler-tagged portion because it will spoil the book for you. I cannot properly explain my opinion without spoilers and because my opinion is not in line with most, I need to go there.**<br/><br/>This is a puzzling mystery but the pacing was too slow in the beginning or perhaps it just took too long to get to the action and then once it got there, it rea</span>
  <span id="freeText13937240143189792338" style="display:none">**If you haven't read this book, I recommend you not read reviews until you have finished the book. If you disregard my suggestion, please don't read my spoiler-tagged portion because it will spoil the book for you. I cannot properly explain my opinion without spoilers and because my opinion is not in line with most, I need to go there.**<br /><br />This is a puzzling mystery but the pacing was too slow in the beginning or perhaps it just took too long to get to the action and then once it got there, it really stretched the limits of what is believable. There was a lot going on in this and I'm not sure every storyline was resolved. This deserves high marks for being smart, tricky, and entertaining. I listened to this audiobook. It was not merely a narration but a performance and it was convincing. It made me feel some passionate disdain but I never really felt the shock and sadness I expected to feel. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This, of course, was because the mother of the child had almost no voice in this story. I'm not sure the story could've handled another voice, but without her voice a crucial piece was missing. I loathed Ian from the word go. His cocky, patronizing, misogynistic air brought out a visceral reaction in me. I could feel myself tensing as soon as I realized he was speaking and I found his matter-of-a-fact retelling of horrible physical and mental abuse off putting. That is excellent characterization! With that said, the ongoing graphic descriptions of the abuse he inflicted took something away from this story. After it was well-established, it began to feel like too much. Then asking me to believe after everything else that Jacob happened to be crossing this street that Ian just happened to turn on in the pouring rain in a fit of rage while abusing his wife without even realizing where he was...and the added identity...that took it over the top for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I understand why others are so drawn to this debut. I agree that it was quite good, atmospheric, and a different sort of story but I couldn't quite get to loving it. Be kind to me, friends! 3.5 stars</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563825419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16513735520713402104">This wasn't an emotionally easy book to take in. Saying that it's heavy would be an understatement, but it's one that is such an incredibly crafted story that I know it's one that will stay on my favorites list for years to come. <br/><br/>Jacob, a young boy, has been hit by a speeding car on a dark and rainy night. The driver, rather than stopping, speeds away leaving the boy's mother traumatized and distraught. Not knowing how to handle her own grief, she flees in effort to escape everything that has ju</span>
  <span id="freeText16513735520713402104" style="display:none">This wasn't an emotionally easy book to take in. Saying that it's heavy would be an understatement, but it's one that is such an incredibly crafted story that I know it's one that will stay on my favorites list for years to come. <br /><br />Jacob, a young boy, has been hit by a speeding car on a dark and rainy night. The driver, rather than stopping, speeds away leaving the boy's mother traumatized and distraught. Not knowing how to handle her own grief, she flees in effort to escape everything that has just unfolded. <br /><br />Who killed Jacob that night? Let me tell you, it wasn't at all who I thought. This book had me guessing literally through the last lines of the epilogue.<br /><br />It's books like this that keep me coming back to the thriller genre over and over again. <br /><br /><b>What did I think?:</b> This is one of the best books I've ever read and the authors ability to craft such a unique web of circumstances is truly an amazing thing. After this, I'd read anything she writes. <br /><br /><b>Who should read it?:</b> This is the best thriller I've read in such a long time, so if it's a genre you enjoy you can't miss this one. I can't wait to discuss it with others who I feel are bound to love it as much as I have. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16513735520713402104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713678601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5815504693825252326"><b>The Hook</b> I’m seeing this everywhere and once again have been drawn in by the hype. IMHO, it is deserved this time. <br/><br/><b>The Line</b> <i>“I want to fix an image of him in my head, but all I can see when I close my eyes is his body, still and lifeless in my arms. I let him go, and I will never forgive myself for that.”</i><br/><br/><b>The Sinker</b> – This is the best fiction I’ve read on this subject since…oh, no, can’t tell you that or it will spoil the whole read for you. Ok, so sometimes I’m an unreliable reviewer. You don’t </span>
  <span id="freeText5815504693825252326" style="display:none"><b>The Hook</b> I’m seeing this everywhere and once again have been drawn in by the hype. IMHO, it is deserved this time. <br /><br /><b>The Line</b> <i>“I want to fix an image of him in my head, but all I can see when I close my eyes is his body, still and lifeless in my arms. I let him go, and I will never forgive myself for that.”</i><br /><br /><b>The Sinker</b> – This is the best fiction I’ve read on this subject since…oh, no, can’t tell you that or it will spoil the whole read for you. Ok, so sometimes I’m an unreliable reviewer. You don’t know where I’m coming from and need to read between the lines to know how I felt about a book. I’ve given up the star ratings and this often leaves you scratching your head. Did she like it or not? <br /><br />Just so you know I really liked <u>I Let You Go</u>. I was hooked right from the gripping prologue. Clare Mackintosh has produced an emotional read with a tenseness that can’t be denied. As I approached the end my senses were being pulled all over the place. I couldn’t turn the pages fast enough. <br /><br />With that said, I don’t know why I think I know better than the author. She made her bed and I didn’t necessarily want to lie or is that lay or whatever, in it. I forgave her the choices made. <br /><br />Though I have gone the route of lightness, make no mistake; this is not a lightweight read. Do not read the jacket or the reviews if you do not want spoilers though thankfully most of my GR friends were very careful. Just read the book. It’s good. I’m adding myself to Clare Mackintosh’s fan base. <br /></span>

See all my Tornado Warnings at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.booksbejeweled'>www.booksbejeweled</a><br/><br/><i>“A tragic accident. It all happened so quickly.   <span id="freeText16664479085741444250" style="display:none">ONE OF MY TOP TEN TWISTERS! See all my Tornado Warnings at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.booksbejeweled">www.booksbejeweled</a><br /><br /><i>“A tragic accident. It all happened so quickly. She couldn’t have prevented it. Could she?”</i><br /><br />Clare Macintosh, the author of I Let You Go, is the real deal. According to her Goodreads profile, she spent twelve years in the police force, including time in the criminal investigations unit (CID). She knows what she is writing about.<br /><br />I Let You Go, her debut novel, was the fastest-selling title by a new crime writer in 2015 (U.K.). It won all kinds of awards and is still an extremely popular book. For good reason.<br /><br />Here’s what it’s about: after a tragic accident, Jenna Gray’s only hope is to start afresh—and in a tiny, remote Welsh village it seems possible, just for a moment, that she might be able to find a new life. But her grief isn’t going to stay in the past for long… THAT IS ALL I CAN TELL YOU without spoilers.<br /><br />This book checks all my required boxes for a top notch domestic thriller!<br /><br />UK setting (SO MUCH LOVE)<br />Heavy on the psychological aspects (YES)<br />Just enough police procedural<br />Sympathetic protagonist<br />Unreliable narrators (MUST HAVE)<br />Breath taking plot twists<br />Compelling mystery (UNPUTDOWNABLE)<br />Expertly-cleverly-plotted writing (TECHNICAL TERM)<br /><br />DING DING DING…..We have a winner! The book takes a minute to set up and you may find it a bit slow, but relax, you’re in good hands. (And wake up! You might want to really pay attention at the beginning since there may or may not be a few clues already sprinkled in. )<br /><br />I found this book compelling and irresistible. Although the subject matter is heavy, it carries an important message and Clare Macintosh is up to the challenge.<br /><br /></span>

  <b>“I only let go for a second.”</b>
</i><br/>Every mother's worst nightmare come true.<br/><br/>This story opens with an accident that would haunt any mother for the rest of her life. Walking home from school on a rainy day, an excited little boy named Jacob pulls away from his mother's hand to cross the street.<br/><br/>At that same moment, a car swerves on the wet pavement, hitting the 5-year-old, killing him instantly. A heartbroken Jenna moves to a remote cottage on the Welsh coast in an attempt to heal and start over.<br/><br/>The </span>

  <b>“I only let go for a second.”</b>
</i><br />Every mother's worst nightmare come true.<br /><br />This story opens with an accident that would haunt any mother for the rest of her life. Walking home from school on a rainy day, an excited little boy named Jacob pulls away from his mother's hand to cross the street.<br /><br />At that same moment, a car swerves on the wet pavement, hitting the 5-year-old, killing him instantly. A heartbroken Jenna moves to a remote cottage on the Welsh coast in an attempt to heal and start over.<br /><br />The rumors are true. There's a HUGE twist about halfway through the book which leaves you breathless and disoriented until your mind catches up with what you just read.<br /><br />This is an extremely impressive debut novel which nabbed the Theakston Old Peculier Crime Novel of the Year Award in the UK.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1821186977" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1821186977?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=british-author">british-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=british-novels">british-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=crime-novel">crime-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=detective-story">detective-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821186977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10972630335104582910">WHERE ARE WE?<br/><br/>Penfach on the Welsh Gower Peninsula. Wales. Yes. <br/><br/>There's some dragging clichés to establish the plot, characters and background, sure. And then there's a chick-lit lite cocktail to endure, and a main character that is too much of a Barbara Cartland English Rose kind of lookalike. Oy, please NO! NO! NO!, love, NO!<br/><br/><b>BUT</b>............'lo and behold! ..........there's the absolute tragedy of a mother losing a child in an accident. <br/><br/>The first part of the story, while the plot heats up, was b</span>
  <span id="freeText10972630335104582910" style="display:none">WHERE ARE WE?<br /><br />Penfach on the Welsh Gower Peninsula. Wales. Yes. <br /><br />There's some dragging clichés to establish the plot, characters and background, sure. And then there's a chick-lit lite cocktail to endure, and a main character that is too much of a Barbara Cartland English Rose kind of lookalike. Oy, please NO! NO! NO!, love, NO!<br /><br /><b>BUT</b>............'lo and behold! ..........there's the absolute tragedy of a mother losing a child in an accident. <br /><br />The first part of the story, while the plot heats up, was blehhhhh. Predictable. Too chick-lit-formulaic. Way too relaxing for the reader. But in retrospect I think it was done intentional, especially to keep the police characters as 'normal' as possible. It drove me crazy though. The suspense....<br /><br />However, when the plot finally kicks in in the second half and starts boilin', with one surprise after the other, the atmosphere turns into a suspense thriller, with a psychological onslaught of shocking, unbearable magnitude.<br /><br />By the time the epilogue calms the reader down, the stars have been piling up. I have just been traumatized and terrorized by a emotional tsunami and survived to share the experience. Let's face it, the British authors know how to drag me through the wringers. I love it!<br /><br />For a debut novel this was an excellent book, give or take my nonexistent admiration for helpless, innocent rose-cheeked, Jenna. Also, the personal experience of the author which triggered this story, the heartbreaking memories she had to go through, makes this experience authentic and true. <br /><br />RECOMMENDED!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10972630335104582910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715405363?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715405363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17848654834640246820"><br/><b> 3.5 stars <br/><br/>What a page turner! </b><br/><br/>I let you go by Clare Mackintosh was one of those books that pulls you in from the first chapter. Its an addictive and wonderfully layered thriller that is suspenseful and a satisfying psychological read.<br/><br/>For some reason I had passed on this novel so many time despite numerous good reviews from friends. I am not sure the blurb or cover appealed to me but decided to pick it up for a summer read and I have to say I really enjoyed the Novel.<br/><br/>It was a slow build up and y</span>
  <span id="freeText17848654834640246820" style="display:none"><br /><b> 3.5 stars <br /><br />What a page turner! </b><br /><br />I let you go by Clare Mackintosh was one of those books that pulls you in from the first chapter. Its an addictive and wonderfully layered thriller that is suspenseful and a satisfying psychological read.<br /><br />For some reason I had passed on this novel so many time despite numerous good reviews from friends. I am not sure the blurb or cover appealed to me but decided to pick it up for a summer read and I have to say I really enjoyed the Novel.<br /><br />It was a slow build up and yet it held my interest from page one. The Characters are interesting, the plot is strong with plenty of suspense and its the sort of book you could read cover to cover in one day just to find out what happens..........<br />Its one of those Novels <i>,<b> Where The Least Said The Better</b></i>, as best to just go in blind.<br /><br />A page turner with lots of twists and turns for readers who enjoy mystery/thrillers style novels.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17848654834640246820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xzo2RmtnHEu/RiJvolgG6p/zT7VqsBWS2ynl+Lr3NtKvkrw8IgLuQJrCcfKZm20T6LrR8WlX1dK1IzgrlvqZDA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bnh36NczUVKSl1/SupflzBvSMa2CaVS5qroXFs4kbWwG0P2SnlajWbcTDE+BVI41bJuv6YGOlPnEsMrF4inCsg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer7141083503328789184">Clare Mackintosh spent twelve years in the police force, leaving in 2011 to write full-time. She lives in North Wales with her husband and their three children.<br/><br/>Her novels have all been Sunday Times top ten bestsellers.<br/><br/>Clare is the patron of the Silver Star Society, an Oxford-based charity which supports the work carried out in the John Radcliffe Hospital's Silver Star unit, providing special care </span>
  <span id="freeText7141083503328789184" style="display:none">Clare Mackintosh spent twelve years in the police force, leaving in 2011 to write full-time. She lives in North Wales with her husband and their three children.<br /><br />Her novels have all been Sunday Times top ten bestsellers.<br /><br />Clare is the patron of the Silver Star Society, an Oxford-based charity which supports the work carried out in the John Radcliffe Hospital's Silver Star unit, providing special care for mothers with medical complications during pregnancy.</span>
